Summary of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis Results

Recent analysis of AI transformation (AX) trends in the manufacturing industry has revealed a key trend where AI technology is spreading beyond factory automation to intelligence and the entire supply chain. This presents new challenges alongside improvements in productivity.

The main trends can be summarized into three categories. First, the intelligence of factories is accelerating. AI-based anomaly detection and predictive maintenance (PdM) based on real-time data analysis are becoming widespread, and the transition to next-generation production systems such as digital twins, which replicate physical factories in virtual spaces, and 'Software-Defined Factories (SDF)', which control processes with software, is active.

Second, the advancement of AI-based process automation. Imitation learning robots that perform tasks by learning human behavior, or AI technology that automatically generates complex tool paths, are significantly increasing the applicability of robots in the field.

Third, the expansion of AI application across the entire supply chain. AI is playing a key role in predicting supply chain risks and strengthening resilience beyond factory operations, and international cooperation and data regulations are emerging as important variables.

While these changes offer the opportunity to maximize production efficiency, they also present challenges such as responding to cross-border data regulations and securing specialized personnel. For a successful AI transformation, beyond the adoption of individual technologies, an ecosystem-centric strategy encompassing data platform construction, talent development, and partner collaboration will be crucial.

Samsung Electronics is promoting AX across the entire supply chain by combining smart factory advancement for its partners, a 1 trillion KRW ESG fund, and SSAFY talent cultivation. We propose a multi-camera face registration/recognition framework that combines YOLOv8-based face detection with CNN behavioral filtering (gaze, blur, occlusion determination) to reduce recognition errors by 18% even in situations with masks, non-frontal faces, or lighting variations, while achieving real-time performance of over 30 FPS per camera and 95%+ accuracy. It has lowered personal information risks through on-device inference, storing only embeddings, and selective blurring, and provides key operational tuning points such as camera placement, accuracy-latency tradeoffs, and system performance metrics (FAR/FRR). It offers high AX value when integrated with manufacturing site access control, restricted area access management, shift personnel flow management, and PPE compliance monitoring, and has significant potential for future expansion into liveness detection, automatic thresholds, lightweight models, and sensor hybrid systems.

As the integration of AI and trade is expected to expand trade by 34-37% (digital service trade by 42%) by 2040, manufacturing companies should redesign their supply chain and market strategies with AI as a prerequisite, constantly monitor policy risks such as tariffs, export controls, and data transfer, and diversify their sourcing of semiconductors, GPUs, cloud, and data. For the operation of smart factories, remote support, and digital twins, build cloud/edge and data residency architectures tailored to regional data governance, and introduce customs clearance and compliance automation and supply chain visibility tools to raise digital capabilities extending to Tier 2/3 suppliers, thereby reducing trade costs and lead times. Furthermore, considering energy/infrastructure bottlenecks, optimize TCO-based workload deployment, including data center power and renewable energy PPAs, and manage digital divide risks through international cooperation and inclusive investment in the fields of standards, customs clearance, and IP.

The WTO WTR 2025 quantitatively demonstrates that AI lowers trade costs (leading to a 34-37% increase in trade by 2040) and expands digital services trade. According to WTO analysis, AI has the potential to expand trade by 34-37% by 2040 through logistics optimization, automation of regulatory compliance, and removal of language barriers. Therefore, manufacturers should re-prioritize AI adoption in export, procurement, customs clearance, and contract processes as a top priority, and establish BCM (Business Continuity Management) integrated with AI-based weather and flood early warning systems at factories and logistics hubs. As skill premiums are expected to drop by 3-4% due to the automation of medium and highly skilled tasks, roles in process, quality, and SCM should be redesigned, and systematic reskilling/upskilling should be carried out. Furthermore, technology diffusion (increased patent citations) should be accelerated through participation in global innovation networks via digital service trade. EU-India cooperation on semiconductor and heavy industry decarbonization and the rise of nations rich in critical minerals and renewable energy are opportunities for the reallocation of battery and power semiconductor supply chains and diversification of raw material sourcing, as well as a time to proactively respond to standards, certification, and security requirements and ensure regulatory compliance through minimizing vendor lock-in.

The WTO report indicates with figures (a 34-37% increase in trade by 2040) that AI can significantly reduce trade costs by overcoming logistics, regulatory compliance, and language barriers, thereby driving an expansion in manufacturing exports and procurement. CarbonSix's SigmaKit is an imitation learning-based standardized hardware and software package. Compared to traditional robot programming, it simplifies initial setup and product switchover, enabling fast re-teaching and line changeovers in HMLV processes such as film attachment/removal, cable fastening, and machine tending. In particular, even small and medium-sized manufacturers can apply AI robots without professional coding, lowering the entry barrier to automation. When implementing it, it is practical to measure improvements in cycle time, success rate, changeover time, and FPY/OEE with a PoC, and also verify PLC/MES integration, safety standards, sensor reliability, and vendor maturity (references/support).

CarbonSix's SigmaKit is an imitation learning-based standardized robot kit that integrates vision, gripper, and teaching tools, supporting rapid setup and re-teaching without expert programming. CarbonSix's SigmaKit provides imitation learning-based robot teaching as a standardized package that integrates precision grippers, sensors, and training tools, enabling quick adoption and easy setup without professional programming. An end-to-end workflow is proposed for the lightweighting of stepped drive shafts, which involves applying a biomimetic SHMS metaheuristic, integrating manufacturing and performance constraints such as bending-torsional combined fatigue load (Modified Goodman), diameter steps, and allowable deflection as static penalties, and then verifying through FBD/BMD â†’ Python optimization â†’ ANSYS FEA. Hyundai Motor Group announced that it would respond to demand slowdown and tariff risks through a multi-electrification portfolio encompassing HEV/EV/EREV/FCEV, region-specific localized EVs, next-generation platforms, strengthening SDV, large-scale CAPEX (77.3 trillion won), and global expansion. From a manufacturing perspective, lowering costs and lead times through mixed-model production and modular commonization, as well as a digital thread connecting PLM-MES-Test and an OTA response verification system, are required for SDV implementation. In addition, localization strategies necessitate regional in-house production of batteries and key components, traceability, and management of local content ratios, and the establishment of new process and testing infrastructure is required in preparation for the expansion of FCEV/EREV. To achieve the target operating profit margin (8-9%), the systematic expansion of manufacturing AX levers such as AI-based quality analysis, predictive maintenance, and line balancing simulation is effective.

Huawei's NVIDIA alternative and SuperPOD-class clusters, emerging within the U.S.-China sanctions environment, materialize multi-vendor/regional diversification strategies and on-premise private AI options for manufacturers' AI infrastructure. China's 'de-NVIDIA' and semiconductor self-sufficiency trends demand a shift in manufacturing AI infrastructure from single GPU dependency to multisourcing, and the construction of an accelerator-agnostic stack using ONNX, OpenXLA, PyTorch/XLA, etc., to reduce vendor lock-in and geopolitical risks. Companies with operations in China should proactively conduct early learning/inference PoCs based on local chips like Ascend and Cambricon to benchmark performance, power, and TCO, and concurrently redesign NPU/FPGA-centric edge and on-premise architectures. Simultaneously, proactively respond to lead time and price fluctuations with a dual-routing supply chain strategy that includes export control compliance, AVL diversification, and monitoring SMIC and YMTC's supply capacity and pricing.

The intensification of the US-China semiconductor conflict has led to a clear trend of China accelerating its 'de-NVIDIA' efforts and fostering its domestic AI chip ecosystem. When operating factories/data centers in China, a practical key point is to swiftly establish performance, TCO, and reliability benchmarks for alternative chips such as Huawei Ascend and Cambricon, and to respond to supply-demand uncertainties with an edge/on-premise hybrid architecture. Simultaneously, cost, lead time, and regulatory risks must be proactively managed through export control compliance, supply chain risk monitoring, and a dual-routing strategy.

The transition from reliance on general-purpose GPUs to domain-specific AI chips, when combined with a one-stop design, verification, and manufacturing platform, can lower power, latency, and TCO, and shorten the lead time from Proof of Concept (PoC) to mass production. UWMì˜ ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” ëª¨ë¸Â·ë°ì´í„° í”„ë£¨ë‹ê³¼ ê²½ëŸ‰í™”ë¡œ AIì˜ ì—°ì‚°Â·ì €ì¥ ë¶€ë‹´ì„ ì¤„ì—¬ ì—ë„ˆì§€Â·ì¸í”„ë¼ ë¹„ìš©ì„ ë‚®ì¶”ê³ , í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ ì˜ì¡´ì„ ì¤„ì¸ ì—£ì§€ ì¶”ë¡ ì„ ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ê²Œ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì—ì„  ë¹„ì „ ê²€ì‚¬Â·ì´ìƒíƒì§€Â·ì˜ˆì§€ë³´ì „ì„ ì¹´ë©”ë¼/ê²Œì´íŠ¸ì›¨ì´ì—ì„œ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ ì²˜ë¦¬í•˜ê³ , ì •í™•ë„ í—ˆìš©í­ì„ ì •í•œ í”„ë£¨ë‹â€“ì •ë°€ë„ ì¶•ì†Œâ€“ì§€ì‹ì¦ë¥˜ ì¡°í•©ê³¼ ì—ì§€ MLOps(KPI: ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬, ì²˜ë¦¬ëŸ‰, inferences/W, ì˜¨ë„)ë¡œ ì„±ëŠ¥â€“ì •í™•ë„ ê· í˜•ê³¼ ìš´ì˜ ì•ˆì •ì„±ì„ í™•ë³´í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. UWM's research reduces AI's computational and storage burden through model and data pruning and lightweighting, thereby lowering energy and infrastructure costs and enabling edge inference with reduced cloud dependency. In manufacturing sites, vision inspection, anomaly detection, and predictive maintenance are processed in real-time on cameras/gateways, and a balance between performance and accuracy and operational stability can be secured through a combination of pruning, precision reduction, and knowledge distillation with a defined accuracy tolerance, along with Edge MLOps (KPIs: memory, throughput, inferences/W, temperature).

Along with the news of UWM and MS collaboration, the key point is that AI pruning can reduce data processing and storage, thereby saving energy and costs, and strengthening local inference at the edge. The manufacturing industry can lighten on-site AI for applications such as vision inspection and predictive maintenance, thereby reducing network dependency and latency, and lowering the burden of data center usage, electricity, and water resources. In practice, an effective approach involves setting an accuracy tolerance, then combining pruning, quantization, and knowledge distillation, managing inferences/W, memory, and latency as KPIs, and standardizing remote updates and on-site verification with edge MLOps.

In manufacturing, AI performance depends not on short-term model performance but on long-term roadmaps and foundational capabilities. Therefore, data infrastructure, governance, MLOps/data engineering, and talent must be proactively established, and the quality, accessibility, and integration of operational data such as MES/ERP/SCADA must be secured. Pilots should include clear KPIs and ROI measurement designs for factors like defect rates, equipment utilization (OEE), and energy costs. Rather than one-off PoCs, phased expansion from pilot â†’ line/factory expansion â†’ standardization should be pursued, with a cross-functional team equipped with data lineage and model monitoring being responsible for operational stability.

Practically, the key tasks are 1) establishing a data backbone plan that integrates equipment, MES, and SCADA data, 2) pilot application of agent-based decision-making (dispatching, anomaly response), 3) real-time data linkage of energy, yield, and waste KPIs, and 4) establishing OT/IT integration, standardization, and edge-cloud pipelines. Posters/sessions are useful for understanding implementation directions and vendor ecosystems in semiconductor fabs to specify PoC topics; however, detailed cases and quantitative results are limited.

This content reflects an industry trend to strengthen the standardization, automation, and sharing of specification data through a 'spec-first' approach centered on packaging/product specifications and the application of AI (LLM-assisted, IDP). The 3M Supplier Responsibility Code serves as a guideline that concretizes the AX roadmap for manufacturing plants, presenting integrated EHS/ESG data pipelines and dashboards, real-time monitoring of process and environmental IoT, traceability linked to PLM/ERP/MES, and regular auditâ€“corrective and preventive action (CAPA) workflows as essential capabilities. Additionally, by requiring AI governanceâ€”including AI usage transparency, pre-approval, and data source managementâ€”and digital verification systems for human rights and labor, it enables the automation and quantification of regulatory compliance and performance management across the entire supply chain.

The 3M Supplier Responsibility Code specifies the human rights, safety, environment, ethics, and management system requirements that manufacturers must possess. From an AX perspective, this requires a digital foundation for continuous collection, tracking, and reporting of EHS/ESG data, real-time monitoring by IoT sensors, a tracking system for responsible minerals and forest raw materials including geographic information, electronic proof for verification of working hours, wages, and age, periodic audit and corrective action workflows, and the establishment of AI governance with pre-approval and transparency at its core. As a result, data governance and dashboards connecting MES/ERP/PLM-GRC-EHS platforms, automated supply chain change notification and evaluation, and transportation and energy optimization analysis are practical directions that simultaneously achieve compliance and performance improvement.

The PReMI 2025 accepted paper list presents a technology landscape directly connected to manufacturing AX: vision-based quality inspection (anomaly detection, low-light, super-resolution, hyperspectral, synthetic data), sensor data predictive maintenance, edge deployment through federated learning and lightweighting, picking/assembly automation using reinforcement learning, high-speed pose estimation, and SLAM, worker assistance based on KG/RAG, Transformer/Graph models, enhanced safety and compliance with SHAP and PPE/OT IDS, and supply chain analysis including Bayesian inventory and HS code classification. We recommend the following as priority PoCs from a field perspective: 1) data augmentation + anomaly detection vision inspection, 2) absorption of defect distribution variations through federated learning across factories, 3) high-speed pose estimation benchmarking and edge accelerator application for picking/placement cells, and 4) construction of GraphRAG based on manuals and maintenance history.
ìš”ì•½:Summary:
ì´ ê¸€ì€ ì œì¡°ì— ì§ì ‘ ì ìš© ê°€ëŠ¥í•œ ì£¼ì œ(ê¸ˆì† ì œì¡° ë¹„ì „ ê²€ì‚¬ìš© ì´ìƒ íƒì§€/ì¦ê°•, í”¼í‚¹&í”Œë ˆì´ìŠ¤ ìì„¸ ì¶”ì •, PPE ê°ì§€)ì™€ ì¸ì ‘ ê¸°ìˆ (ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµ, RAG/KG, ë² ì´ì§€ì•ˆ ì¬ê³ ê´€ë¦¬, ì—£ì§€Â·ê²½ëŸ‰ AI)ì„ í­ë„“ê²Œ í¬ê´„í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê°œë³„ ë…¼ë¬¸ì˜ ì„¸ë¶€ ê²°ê³¼ëŠ” ì—†ì§€ë§Œ, í’ˆì§ˆÂ·ìë™í™”Â·ê³µê¸‰ë§Â·ì•ˆì „Â·ë³´ì•ˆÂ·ì„¤ëª…ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì—ì„œì˜ ìš°ì„  íˆ¬ì ì˜ì—­ê³¼ PoC ë°©í–¥ì„ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ ì‹ë³„í•˜ëŠ” ë° ìœ ìš©í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì œì¡°ì‚¬ëŠ” ì‹œê° ê²€ì‚¬ ê³ ë„í™”, ê³µì¥ ê°„ ì—°í•©í•™ìŠµ, ê³ ì† ë¡œë´‡ ìì„¸ ì¶”ì •, ë¬¸ì„œ ê¸°ë°˜ GraphRAG, ì•ˆì „Â·ë³´ì•ˆ í†µí•© PoCë¥¼ ìš°ì„  ì¶”ì§„í•  ê°€ì¹˜ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. This article broadly covers topics directly applicable to manufacturing (anomaly detection/augmentation for vision inspection in metal manufacturing, picking & place pose estimation, PPE detection) and adjacent technologies (federated learning, RAG/KG, Bayesian inventory management, edge/lightweight AI). While there are no detailed results from individual papers, it is useful for quickly identifying priority investment areas and PoC directions in quality, automation, supply chain, safety, security, and explainability. Manufacturers should prioritize advanced visual inspection, inter-factory federated learning, high-speed robot pose estimation, document-based GraphRAG, and integrated safety/security PoCs.

ë™ë°˜ì„±ì¥Â·SV ê²½ì˜ì„ ìš´ì˜ ì›ë¦¬ë¡œ ì‚¼ê³  ìƒìƒí€ë“œÂ·ì¡°ê¸°ì§€ê¸‰Â·ì„±ê³¼ì—°ë™ ê¸ˆìœµì„ ì ìš©í•˜ë©´ í˜‘ë ¥ì‚¬ í˜„ê¸ˆíë¦„ ì•ˆì •â†’ë‚©ê¸°Â·í’ˆì§ˆ ê°œì„ â†’ê³µë™ R&Dë¡œ ì´ì–´ì§€ëŠ” ì„ ìˆœí™˜ì„ ë§Œë“¤ì–´ ê³µê¸‰ë§ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ë‚®ì¶œ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ê·¸ë£¹ ì°¨ì›ì˜ AIÂ·ë°ì´í„° ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ì™€ íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆ ê¸°ìˆ ì—­ëŸ‰ ê°•í™”(ë””ì§€í„¸ ê³µì •, í’ˆì§ˆ/ì„¤ë¹„ ë°ì´í„° í‘œì¤€, ì‚¬ì´ë²„ë³´ì•ˆ) ë° ë²¤ì²˜-í´ë¼ì´ì–¸íŠ¸í˜• ì˜¤í”ˆì´ë…¸ë² ì´ì…˜ì„ ê²°í•©í•˜ë©´ ìˆ˜ìœ¨Â·ì˜ˆì§€ë³´ì „Â·ì—ë„ˆì§€ ìµœì í™” ë“± ì œì¡° AX ì„±ê³¼ê°€ ê°€ì†ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì‹¤í–‰ í¬ì¸íŠ¸ëŠ” ìƒìƒ KPIì˜ C-level ë³´ìƒ ì—°ë™, í˜‘ë ¥ì‚¬ ì„±ìˆ™ë„ ì§„ë‹¨ê³¼ ë‹¨ê³„ë³„ ì§€ì›, ë©€í‹°ì†Œì‹±ê³¼ ë¶ë¯¸/EU ê·œì œ ëŒ€ì‘í˜• ESG ë°ì´í„° íˆ¬ëª…í™”ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. By adopting Shared Growth and SV Management as operating principles and applying mutual growth funds, early payments, and performance-linked financing, a virtuous cycle can be created leading to stable cash flow for partners, improved delivery times and quality, and joint R&D, thereby reducing supply chain risks. When group-level AI and data governance, the strengthening of partner technical capabilities (digital processes, quality/equipment data standards, cybersecurity), and venture-client type open innovation are combined, manufacturing AX performance, such as yield, predictive maintenance, and energy optimization, will be accelerated. Key action points include linking C-level compensation to mutual growth KPIs, diagnosing partner maturity and providing phased support, multi-sourcing, and enhancing the transparency of ESG data to comply with North American/EU regulations.

Since the NVIDIA-Intel $5 billion collaboration will impact CPU selection for data center servers, platform standards, and the proliferation of AI PCs, manufacturers should re-evaluate their Intel-AMD dual-vendor benchmarks and performance-power-TCO models based on AI/simulation workloads, and adjust their specification roadmaps for on-site edge laptops and workstations. ì¤‘êµ­ì˜ ì—”ë¹„ë””ì•„ AI ì¹© êµ¬ë§¤ ê¸ˆì§€ëŠ” ì œì¡° í˜„ì¥ì˜ ë¹„ì „ê²€ì‚¬Â·ì˜ˆì§€ë³´ì „ ë“± AI ì›Œí¬ë¡œë“œì— í•„ìš”í•œ ì—°ì‚°ìì› ê³µê¸‰ë§ì˜ ì§€ì •í•™ì  ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ í‚¤ìš°ë¯€ë¡œ, NVIDIA ë‹¨ì¼ ì˜ì¡´ì„ ì¤„ì´ê³  AMD/Intel/NPU/FPGAì™€ í™”ì›¨ì´ Ascend ë“± ëŒ€ì²´ ì¹©ì„ í¬í•¨í•œ ë©€í‹°ë²¤ë” ì „ëµì„ ë§ˆë ¨í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ëª¨ë¸ ì–‘ìí™”(8/4-bit)Â·í”„ë£¨ë‹Â·ì§€ì‹ì¦ë¥˜ë¡œ ì €ì‚¬ì–‘ ê°€ì†ê¸°ì—ì„œë„ ëª©í‘œ ì •í™•ë„ë¥¼ í™•ë³´í•˜ê³ , ONNX/OpenXLA/ROCm/oneDNN/CANN ë“± ì´ì‹ì„± ìŠ¤íƒê³¼ MLOps í‘œì¤€í™”ë¥¼ í†µí•´ ì¤‘êµ­ í˜„ì§€ í´ë¼ìš°ë“œ(AlibabaÂ·Baidu)ì™€ ì˜¨í”„ë ˆë¯¸ìŠ¤ ì—£ì§€ë¥¼ í˜¼í•© ìš´ìš©í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ì•„í‚¤í…ì²˜ë¥¼ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ì„¸ìš”. ë˜í•œ ì¹© ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„Â·ì „ë ¥/ëƒ‰ê°Â·ì†Œí”„íŠ¸ì›¨ì–´ ì„±ìˆ™ë„ì™€ ê·œì œ ë³€ìˆ˜ë¥¼ ë°˜ì˜í•œ TCO/ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ í”Œë˜ë‹ì„ ìˆ˜í–‰í•˜ê³ , ë¼ì¸ ê°€ë™ë¥ Â·ì¶”ë¡  ì§€ì—°(SLA)Â·ìŠ¤í¬ë©ë¥  ë“± KPIì— ì—°ì‚°ìì› ì œì•½ ë¯¼ê°ë„ë¥¼ ì—°ê²°í•´ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ê´€ë¦¬í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. China's ban on purchasing NVIDIA AI chips increases the geopolitical risk of the compute resource supply chain required for AI workloads such as vision inspection and predictive maintenance in manufacturing sites. Therefore, it is necessary to reduce single reliance on NVIDIA and establish a multi-vendor strategy including alternative chips like AMD/Intel/NPU/FPGA and Huawei Ascend. Ensure target accuracy even on low-spec accelerators through model quantization (8/4-bit), pruning, and knowledge distillation, and build an architecture that can operate a hybrid of China's local clouds (AlibabaÂ·Baidu) and on-premise edge through portable stacks like ONNX/OpenXLA/ROCm/oneDNN/CANN and MLOps standardization. Furthermore, perform TCO/scenario planning that reflects chip lead time, power/cooling, software maturity, and regulatory variables, and manage risk by connecting compute resource constraint sensitivity to KPIs such as line utilization, inference latency (SLA), and scrap rate.

The Chinese government's restrictions on purchasing NVIDIA AI chips highlight the single-vendor dependency risk in manufacturing AI infrastructure. Manufacturers need a heterogeneous computing strategy (including NVIDIA alternatives), a shift to model quantization and lightweighting, an edge-cloud hybrid architecture tailored to local Chinese regulations, and a re-evaluation of TCO, including lead time, power consumption, and software maturity. Additionally, MLOps standardization is required to ensure reproducibility during hardware replacement, along with parallel production KPI sensitivity analysis and scenario planning in response to supply chain changes.
